- **The resilient `plumb serve` heartbeat can no longer SIGKILL a healthy, freshly-respawned daemon.** `runHeartbeat` read the connection generation *after* the ping timed out, so if a pump-driven reconnect bumped the generation during the ping wait, the hang verdict killed the *new* daemon. It now captures the generation *before* sending the ping; a generation mismatch at reconnect time makes the kill a no-op (the existing generation guard fires). Guard: `TestProxyReconnectStaleGenerationDoesNotKill`. `internal/cli/serve_proxy_heartbeat.go`.

## 0.8.14 (2026-05-28)

### Fixed
- **Keyboard navigation in the TUI Sessions (and Memory) panel now scrolls the list to keep the selection on screen.** Pressing ‚Üì past the last visible row moved the selection cursor but the viewport stayed put ‚Äî the selected row scrolled out of view while the cursor kept advancing, so the list looked frozen (mouse-wheel scrolling worked because it drives `leftScroll` directly). The four keyboard handlers (`mainKeyUp`/`mainKeyDown`/`mainKeyPageDown`/`mainKeyPageUp`, `internal/tui/model_keys.go`) reset `m.leftScroll = 0` on every cursor move ‚Äî and `mainKeyPageUp` never touched it at all ‚Äî so the scroll offset never followed the cursor. They now call a new `ensureLeftCursorVisible()` (`internal/tui/model_refresh.go`, beside the popup's existing `ensurePopupCursorVisible`) after the cursor moves: it advances `leftScroll` by the minimum needed to keep the selected row's content lines within the body viewport (accounting for the 2-line panel header and the per-item line count ‚Äî 3 lines per session, 4 per memory), preserves the offset when the selection is already visible (so it never yanks a mouse-scrolled view), and reveals the panel header when the selection returns to the first row. The Memory section (index 2) shares `leftScroll` and the same handlers, so it is fixed by the same helper; the adjustment is keypress-only ‚Äî `refresh()`'s 2 s poll never calls it, so it cannot fight a mouse scroll. Guards: `TestEnsureLeftCursorVisible` (the helper's math across both sections, incl. the already-visible no-yank and last-item clamp cases), `TestSessionsKeyboardScrollFollowsCursor` and `TestMemoryKeyboardScrollFollowsCursor` (handler wiring ‚Äî holding ‚Üì/‚Üë/pgdn/pgup keeps the selection visible).

## 0.8.13 (2026-05-28)

### Added
- **Session lifecycle: idle detection, eviction, and agent-session linking.** Three related improvements to prevent stale sessions from accumulating and allow a reconnecting agent to resume its previous session identity.
  - **Idle detection** ‚Äî every tool call updates a session's `LastSeenAt` timestamp (via `os.Chtimes` on the session file, so there is no extra JSON decode). `session.List()` populates `LastSeenAt` from the file mtime. The TUI Sessions panel shows a `~` marker on sessions idle for longer than the configurable threshold (default 30 min).
  - **Idle eviction** ‚Äî a background reaper in the daemon (5-min tick) cancels connections whose last tool call was more than the configurable eviction TTL ago (default 60 min). This closes the hanging-session problem where `plumb serve`'s stdio pipe stayed open after the agent stopped talking.
  - **Agent-session linking** ‚Äî `session_start` now accepts an optional `session_id` parameter (an opaque string the agent provides, e.g. a conversation ID). The session persists this as `ExternalID` in its on-disk JSON file. `Unregister` now marks the file with `ended_at` rather than deleting it, keeping it for a 24-hour grace period. When a reconnecting agent passes the same `session_id`, plumb calls `session.FindEnded` to locate the previous session and inherits its name ‚Äî so the TUI shows session continuity across reconnects and `plumb restart`.
  - New `[session]` config section: `idle_threshold_minutes` (default 30) and `eviction_ttl_minutes` (default 60, 0 to disable).

## 0.8.12 (2026-05-27)

### Fixed
- **The `diagnostics` tool no longer returns stale or out-of-scope errors when called with no URI arguments.** Two independent bugs caused false positives that blocked production releases: (1) `routingInvProxy.AllDiagnostics()` returned the primary workspace's entire diagnostic map without filtering by workspace root ‚Äî gopls can emit `publishDiagnostics` for files it transitively analyses (dependency packages, stdlib, or files accessed during indexing that lie outside the workspace root), and all of these accumulated in the invalidator unfiltered. `AllDiagnostics()` now restricts the returned map to URIs whose path falls under the primary workspace root (`uriUnderRoot`, same logic as the per-URI routing already used by `Diagnostics(uri)`). (2) The `Invalidator` stored diagnostics without timestamps, so if a file changed on disk (e.g. after a successful `make build`) before gopls had re-published a clean `publishDiagnostics` notification, the cached stale errors were returned with no warning whatsoever. The `Invalidator` now records a `time.Time` per URI on every `publishDiagnostics` push (`diagTimes` map); when `diagnostics` is called with no arguments, it compares each file's current on-disk mtime against its diagnostic timestamp and annotates any file whose mtime is newer with `(file modified after last analysis ‚Äî may be stale)`, plus a workspace-level `Note: N file(s) modified since last analysis` header so the caller knows to wait for the language server to finish re-analysing. The `timedDiagnosticsSource` interface opt-in (type assertion) keeps the new staleness path invisible to test stubs that implement only the base `diagnosticsSource`. Minor efficiency fix: `singleURI` now uses the new `Tracked(uri) bool` method to check whether a URI has ever been reported on, instead of copying the entire diagnostic map via `AllDiagnostics()` just to do a key lookup.

## 0.8.11 (2026-05-27)

### Added
- **Member-level extraction is now consistent across every code extractor ‚Äî struct fields, class properties and module/class bindings are indexed uniformly, closing a recall gap where Rust/Zig/TypeScript/JavaScript surfaced no fields at all and Python surfaced no constants or variables.** A single documented contract (`docs/internal/extractor-conventions.md`) now governs every tree-sitter extractor: a value-holding member of a code type ‚Üí `KindConstant` when declared immutable (`final`/`val`/`let`/`const`/`readonly`/Python ALL_CAPS) else `KindVariable`, contained in its type at confidence 1.0; `KindField` is reserved for data-format keys/columns (SQL/TOML/YAML). Brought into line: **Rust** struct/union fields (‚Üí variable), `impl` associated `const`/`type` (‚Üí constant/type, via the existing deferred 0.8 impl‚Üítype link), and enum variants (‚Üí constant, which Rust previously did not extract at all); **Zig** container fields (‚Üí variable) and enum members (‚Üí constant); **TypeScript** class properties and interface property signatures (`readonly`‚Üíconstant, else variable); **JavaScript** class fields incl. `#private`/`static` (‚Üí variable); **Python** module- and class-level bindings (ALL_CAPS‚Üíconstant, else variable), with a new `inFunc` guard so function-locals are still never surfaced. Java/Swift/Kotlin already conformed (final/let/val‚Üíconstant). **YAML** keys are now path-qualified (`services.web.image`) to match the SQL/TOML `Qualified` convention. Per-language guard tests added for each (`Test{Rust,Zig,TypeScript,JavaScript,Python}_‚Ä¶Fields‚Ä¶`, `TestYAML_QualifiedDottedPath`).
- **Generic grammar-regression guards for all 15 tree-sitter extractors.** `TestExtractors_ParseFidelity` (table-driven) asserts each extractor's idiomatic sample parses with 0 ERROR/MISSING nodes **and** still emits its trailing declaration ‚Äî generalising the TypeScript typed-arrow cascade guard so a future gotreesitter bump that regresses any grammar fails loudly, not silently. `TestExtractors_MalformedInputNoPanic` feeds each extractor garbage and asserts no panic (complementing the existing `safeExtract` daemon backstop). New `TestBuildExtractorsCoversRegistry` closes a silent-failure seam ‚Äî a `langsupport` row added without an `extractorCtors` constructor (which would stop that language being indexed with no error) now fails the build's tests ‚Äî and `TestExtractorRegistryAlignment` pins each extractor's `Extensions()` and `Language()` label to its registry row (documenting the intentional `tsx`-row ‚Üí `Language()=="typescript"` alias).

### Fixed
- **The LSP-down symbol fallback no longer resolves a `Receiver.Method` name by substring, which could pick the wrong symbol.** `topologyNodeByPath`/`topologyNodesByName` (`internal/tools/symbol_topology_fallback.go`) matched the receiver/parent with `strings.Contains(n.Qualified, parent)`, so `User.Save` could match `(SuperUser).Save`. They now match a whole identifier segment (`qualifiedHasSegment`, splitting on non-identifier runes), preserving Go's `(*Receiver).Method` form while rejecting the substring false positive. Guard: `TestReadSymbol_TopologyFallback_ReceiverSegmentNotSubstring`.
- **`topology_affected` reliably finds a changed file's co-located tests, even when the file's path does not surface through FTS5.** `resolveAffectedRoots` searched the index for the file *path string* and matched on the result ‚Äî so a file whose symbols did not rank for that query yielded no root, and its sibling tests were silently under-reported (the tool's headline "I changed these files, which tests?" case). It now resolves file inputs deterministically via `Store.SymbolsInFile` and always seeds the file's directory for the co-location pass, falling back to the search only when the path is not indexed. Guard: `TestTopologyAffected_FileRootSeedsColocation`.
- **Rust and Zig no longer surface function-local bindings as module-level symbols.** A `const`/`static`/`type` declared inside a Rust `fn` body, and a `const`/`var` inside a Zig function, were extracted as if top-level ‚Äî every other extractor already excluded locals (Python gained the same guard above). Both now thread an `inFunc` flag through their walk so only nested `fn`s and (Rust) `use` imports surface from inside a function; all other in-function declarations are skipped. This makes the "locals are not surfaced" line in `docs/internal/extractor-conventions.md` true for every extractor. Guards: the cross-language `TestExtractors_MemberConventions` (immutable‚Üíconstant, mutable‚Üívariable, function-local‚Üíabsent, run across Java/Swift/Kotlin/Rust/Zig/JavaScript/TypeScript/Python), plus `TestRust_UnionFieldsAndEnumVariants` and `TestTypeScript_PrivateAndStaticFields`.

### Changed
- **The `findExtractor` / `langsupport.ByPath` extension-and-basename matcher is now a single shared function** (`langsupport.MatchExtPattern`), removing the duplicated 4-line copy in `internal/topology/extractor.go` so the two can no longer drift. `topology.KindField`'s doc was corrected to reserve it for data-format keys/columns (it previously claimed "struct fields", which the OO extractors never emitted).

## 0.8.10 (2026-05-26)

### Fixed
- **The first symbol/LSP call to a cold or large workspace no longer hangs for minutes (Claude Desktop's 4-minute "no result received" timeout) ‚Äî it returns within ~2 s, falling back to the tree-sitter index while the language server warms up in the background.** `workspacePool.acquireLang` (`internal/cli/pool.go`) ran `sup.Start(ctx)` ‚Äî the full gopls/pyright `initialize`+`initialized` cold-start handshake ‚Äî **synchronously while holding the pool mutex**, with no deadline (the 30 s `[lsp_query] timeout` / `withLSPDeadline` only wraps the *query*, which never got to run). So the very first path-bearing tool call (via `onBeforeTool ‚Üí attachWorkspace`, or `route`) blocked until the client gave up, and the held `p.mu` stalled every other workspace operation meanwhile. On a large Go monorepo (gopls walking the module) or a Rust project (rust-analyzer running `cargo metadata`) this was a reliable multi-minute hang ‚Äî `read_symbol` was the most-reported victim, even though it already has a tree-sitter fallback that the hang made unreachable (the block happened *before* the tool body ran). Fix: acquisition is now **non-blocking and background-warmed**. The new `Supervisor.StartAsync` (`internal/lsp/supervisor.go`) spawns the supervision loop without waiting on the first handshake; `acquireLang` publishes the pool entry under the lock and then **releases the mutex before any wait**, so concurrent acquires for the same root reuse the one warming entry and a server is never spawned twice. It waits only a short, bounded `firstStartGrace` (2 s) inline ‚Äî long enough that a small/warm project still gets full LSP results on the first call ‚Äî then returns the not-yet-ready entry; `proxy.get()` stays nil (which the routing proxy already surfaces as "LSP server not yet ready"), so the fallback-capable tools (`read_symbol`, `find_symbol`, `workspace_symbols`, `list_symbols`, `file_outline`) degrade to the topology / fresh tree-sitter parse instead of blocking, and the position/semantic tools return a fast, honest error the agent can retry once the server warms up. A first-start failure (e.g. a missing binary) still returns fast and removes the dead entry so a later call retries ‚Äî preserving the `attachWorkspace` degrade-to-`LanguageNone` path. **Latent bug also fixed:** supervisors now run on the **daemon-lifetime context** (threaded into `newWorkspacePool`), not the first caller's request context ‚Äî the pool is shared across connections, so tying a server's lifetime to one connection's context risked tearing it down for everyone when that connection disconnected. Guards: `TestSupervisor_StartAsync_ReadyThenStop` / `_SpawnFailureNoRetry` / `_SlowOnStart` / `_AbandonedReadyChan`, `TestSupervisor_Start_Sync`(`_Failure`), and `TestAcquireLang_ConcurrentReusesSingleEntry` / `_FirstStartFailureRemovesEntry` / `_CancelledCtxKeepsWarming`.

## 0.8.9 (2026-05-26)

### Fixed
- **The daemon now shuts down cleanly within a bounded time of `SIGTERM`, so a slow or hung language server can no longer stall a restart ‚Äî and the F1 SIGKILL becomes a rare last resort rather than the common path.** The shutdown path had no deadline anywhere: `workspacePool.close` (`internal/cli/pool.go`) called `lsp.Shutdown(context.Background())` before killing the process, so a cold/indexing gopls (or a rust-analyzer running `cargo metadata`) blocked daemon exit indefinitely; `runDaemonAcceptLoop` then did an unbounded `wg.Wait()` for in-flight connections; and nothing guaranteed the process ever exited. A daemon stuck in any of these outlived `stopByPID`'s 5 s poll while still holding the lifetime `plumb.daemon.lock`, so `respawnDaemon` could not bind the socket and timed out ‚Äî and the F1 escalation then `SIGKILL`'d it, interrupting gopls/topology mid-flight (orphaned children, a topology WAL write cut short). Fix, defence-in-depth: (1) `close` now tears entries down **concurrently under a bounded `poolCloseGrace` (2 s)** via the new `closeEntry`, which runs the best-effort `Shutdown`/`Exit` handshake under that deadline (jsonrpc honours `ctx`, so a hung server unblocks) and then **always** calls `sup.Stop()` ‚Äî cancelling the supervisor's `exec.CommandContext` is the real guarantee the process dies; (2) the accept loop drains in-flight connections under `acceptDrainGrace` (2 s) via the new `drainConnections` instead of waiting forever; (3) a last-resort `armShutdownWatchdog` forces `os.Exit(0)` `shutdownHardDeadline` (5 s) after a signal cancels the daemon context, so even a wedged teardown step releases the lock promptly (the kernel drops the flock on process death). Clean, prompt shutdown is now the norm; F1's `forceKillIfAlive` only fires on genuine pathology. Guards: `TestCloseEntry_BoundsHungShutdown`, `TestArmShutdownWatchdog_ForcesExitAfterDeadline`, `TestArmShutdownWatchdog_NoExitWhileServing`, `TestDrainConnections`.
- **The resilient `plumb serve` proxy no longer double-responds to (or silently replays) a request sent during a reconnect.** `pumpClientToDaemon` added every request to the in-flight `outstanding` set *before* writing it to the daemon. If that write then failed (the daemon died mid-frame, or the connection was nil during an in-progress reconnect), the reconnect's `failOutstanding` synthesised a retryable `-32000` for the request **and** the pump's retry loop re-sent the same frame to the fresh daemon ‚Äî so the client received two responses for one id, and a non-idempotent write (`edit_file`, `git commit`) executed despite the "please retry" error, contradicting the documented "writes are never auto-replayed" guarantee. The frame's handshake capture (needed for replay) is now split from request tracking: `captureHandshake` still runs before the write, but the new `trackOutstanding` records a request only *after* its write to the daemon succeeds. A request whose write failed never reached a daemon, so it is simply re-sent once; a confirmed-sent request the daemon dies before answering still gets exactly one `-32000`. Guard: `TestProxyOutstandingTrackedOnlyAfterSend`.
- **The `plumb serve` hang-detector now kills only the daemon it was connected to, not whatever PID the file currently holds.** `killHungDaemon` read `plumb.pid` *at kill time*, so if a hung daemon had already been replaced (by this client's own reconnect, or another client's), the heartbeat could SIGKILL the **freshly-spawned** daemon ‚Äî disconnecting everyone again. The proxy now captures the connected daemon's PID from the file after each (re)connect (`reconnectingProxy.daemonPID`) and the hang path kills exactly that PID; a PID already gone is a no-op. The `plumb.spawn.lock` already serialises spawns, so the kill targeting its own PID closes the cross-client race. Guard: `TestProxyKillTargetsCapturedPID`.
- **`plumb restart` now escalates to SIGKILL when the daemon ignores SIGTERM, so the restart is real.** `restart` reused `stopByPID` (SIGTERM + a 5 s poll); a daemon that ignored SIGTERM was left running, and `respawnDaemon` then dialled the still-stuck daemon and printed "Daemon restarted" ‚Äî a no-op restart. The restart loop now follows the SIGTERM with `forceKillIfAlive`, which SIGKILLs a still-alive daemon (short grace) so a fresh one genuinely takes its place. `plumb stop` is unchanged ‚Äî it remains the graceful, no-escalation path. Guard: `TestForceKillIfAlive`.

## 0.8.8 (2026-05-26)

### Fixed
- **A live topology enable/disable now takes effect on already-connected sessions, instead of stranding them on a closed index.** When the global config reloads, the daemon-level subscriber runs `topoPool.Reconcile` (which can close or re-open the shared per-root store) ‚Äî but a session's cached `s.topologyStore` pointer was never refreshed, so after a reconcile its `topology_*` tools operated on a **closed** SQLite handle until the session reconnected; and a live *enable* never attached a store to an already-running session at all. Two parts: (1) `config.Store` now notifies listeners in **registration order** (`internal/config/store.go`), so the daemon-level subscriber ‚Äî registered before any connection ‚Äî always reconciles the pool *before* any per-session subscriber runs; (2) each session's reload subscriber calls the new `connSession.reconcileTopologyStore` (`internal/cli/conn.go`), which re-acquires the fresh pooled store when topology is enabled for the workspace (honouring the per-project merge) or clears the pointer when it is disabled. This also makes the TUI Settings "Topology = live" reload tier **accurate** ‚Äî enabling or disabling topology (including from the Settings screen) now applies to the current session, not only the next one ‚Äî so no label change was needed. Guards: `TestStore_NotifiesInRegistrationOrder`, `TestReconcileTopologyStore_EnableDisable`.

## 0.8.7 (2026-05-26)

### Added
- **Live topology indexing via OS-level file watching (`[topology] watch`, default on).** The index now updates the moment a file changes on disk ‚Äî regardless of who changed it: this agent, another agent sharing the daemon, or you in your editor ‚Äî replacing time-based polling, which can only ever be eventually-consistent. A per-workspace watcher (`internal/topology/watcher.go`, built on [`github.com/sgtdi/fswatcher`](https://github.com/sgtdi/fswatcher) v1.3.0 ‚Äî FSEvents on macOS, inotify on Linux, kqueue on the BSDs, ReadDirectoryChangesW on Windows) translates each change into an incremental re-index on the *existing* bounded indexer queue (no second queue). It is robust under a mass change (`git checkout`, a formatter rewriting the tree): the OS cooldown coalesces per path, the indexer's queue coalesces again (last-op-per-path), and on a queue-full or OS-overflow signal it collapses to a single paced full resync rather than a storm ‚Äî so worst-case work is bounded to one resync, never thousands of parallel syncs. `.plumb/` is excluded from watching so the index's own `topology.db`/`-wal`/`-shm` writes can't self-trigger a loop. While the watcher is live the periodic `resync_interval_minutes` poll is **suppressed** (freshness is purely event-driven, with a full resync still run at startup and on any dropped/overflow signal); `resync_interval_minutes` remains the fallback when `watch = false` or the platform watcher cannot start (logged, degrades gracefully ‚Äî never blocks the daemon). New `[topology] watch` config field (default true), hot-reloaded through the existing topology-pool reconcile. Unit tests: `TestFSWatcher_Handle` (event‚Üíaction mapping, incl. the self-trigger and overflow paths), `TestShouldSkipPath`, `TestFSWatcher_StartStop` (real-watcher lifecycle). Dependency added: `github.com/sgtdi/fswatcher` (MIT; pulls `golang.org/x/sys`).

## 0.8.6 (2026-05-26)

### Added
- **The TUI's session shortcuts (`r` rename, `a` refresh) are now discoverable.** They were only the hardcoded `case "r"`/`case "a"` in the key handler ‚Äî absent from the help overlay, the status bar, and the docs ‚Äî so a user had no way to find them. They now surface in two places: a new **"Sessions"** group in the `ctrl+h` help overlay (`renderHelp`), and a **pinned footer at the bottom of the Sessions right panel** ‚Äî a blank spacer above an `r rename  ¬∑  a refresh` hint. The footer rows sit *outside* the scroll viewport: `renderBodySection` reserves `len(footer)` rows, scrolls the panel content within the reduced height, and draws the footer over the bottom rows, so the hint survives scrolling instead of disappearing with the content. `renderBodySection` was decomposed into `sessionsRightFooter`/`bodyColumn`/`rightBodyColumn`/`assembleBodyRow` to stay within the gocyclo-15 contract. One caveat: the new help group makes the `ctrl+h` overlay ~31 rows tall, so it needs a terminal of at least that height to render without top-clipping (was ~27). Docs: `docs/cli-reference.md`. Guards: `TestSessionsRightFooterPinnedAndScrolls` (hint on the last row, blank spacer above, preserved when scrolled, absent in the Memory section) and an extended `TestRenderHelpGroupsShortcutsAndKeepsBorders`.

### Fixed
- **Topology now re-indexes on every write, instead of only on the periodic resync.** `connSession.buildWriteDeps` built the `TopologyNotify` write hook by capturing `s.topologyStore` ‚Äî but `buildWriteDeps` runs during `registerAllTools`, *before* the client handshake attaches the workspace, so the store was always `nil` at capture time and the hook was silently never wired. The index then refreshed only via the periodic `resync_interval_minutes` (default 60) walk, so after an edit `topology_search`/`topology_affected`/`file_outline` saw stale structure for up to an hour ‚Äî undermining the "run `topology_affected` after writing" workflow and the topology-as-default-discovery story. Fix: resolve the store lazily on each write through the new `connSession.topologyStoreLive()` (read under `stateMu`), shared by the write hook and the `topoFn` topology-tool accessor, so a store attached after registration is picked up. Guard: `TestTopologyStoreLive_ReflectsLateAttach` (`internal/cli/conn_topology_test.go`).
- **A per-project `[topology] enabled = false` now actually opts a project out.** `startTopologyIndexer` gated on the *global* `store.Current().Topology.Enabled`, ignoring the project merge ‚Äî so with topology on by default (0.8.5) a project that set `enabled = false` in `<workspace>/.plumb/config.toml` still had `topology.db` created and indexing started, contradicting the documented escape hatch. It now consults the project-merged value via the new `connSession.topologyEnabledFor(workspace)` (`config.LoadProject`), so an explicit project opt-out wins over the global default-on (and a project opt-in wins over a global opt-out). Per-project *tuning* (resync interval, excludes, size caps) remains pool-global ‚Äî tracked in `docs/internal/todo.md`. Guard: `TestTopologyEnabledFor_ProjectOptOutWins`.
- **A topology query that simply matched nothing no longer falsely reports "topology indexing is disabled".** `store.Search` (and the routes/affected paths) return a `nil` slice on zero matches, and each `topology_*` formatter conflated that `nil` with a `nil` (disabled) store ‚Äî so any empty `topology_search`/`topology_routes`/`topology_affected` told the agent topology was off and to set `[topology] enabled = true`, the exact "topology looks broken" misdiagnosis the 0.8.5 default-on was meant to prevent. The "disabled" message now comes from a single explicit `store == nil` check in each tool's `Execute` (shared `topologyDisabledMessage`); a live index with no matches returns a tool-specific "no results"/"not found"/"none ‚Ä¶ in the index" message. Guards: `TestTopologySearch_EmptyResultNotDisabled`, `TestTopologyRoutes_EmptyResultNotDisabled`, `TestTopologyTools_NilStoreStillReportsDisabled`, and the `‚Ä¶_FormatNilResult` tests updated from asserting the buggy behaviour.

## 0.8.5 (2026-05-26)

### Fixed
- **The TUI "Rename Session" modal is now centred over a dimmed background, with a clean right border.** It was the last overlay still hand-rolling its own geometry: `View()` baked in its own `topPad`/`leftPad`, then `renderModal` passed that near-full-screen string to `spliceOverlay` ‚Äî which *re-centres* whatever it is given, so the already-left-padded box was shoved against the right edge (the box's own padding inflated the width `spliceOverlay` measured). The right border was independently ragged because the input row was built with `fmt.Sprintf("‚îÇ  New name: [%-40s‚îÇ", ‚Ä¶)` ‚Äî the padded value plus the literal `]` came out one column wider than every other row. And the background never dimmed because `m.renameModal != nil` was missing from the `isOverlay` flag (`internal/tui/model_render.go`), unlike every sibling overlay. Fix: the modal now follows the help/theme-picker idiom ‚Äî `box()` builds *only* themed, rounded-border (`‚ï≠‚ïÆ‚ï∞‚ïØ`) lines sized to their content and pads every row by `lipgloss.Width` (so styled/multi-byte cells can't desync the border), and `spliceOverlay` alone centres it over the now-dimmed body. Guards: `TestRenameModalBoxWidthsConsistent` (every box line shares one visible width, incl. an 80-char `longinput` case) and `TestRenameModalCentred` (left/right background margins match within a column).
- **`plumb restart`/`plumb stop` no longer leave the old daemon as a `<defunct>` zombie, and no longer print a false "did not stop within 5 seconds" warning.** `startDaemonProcess` (`internal/cli/daemon.go`) ran `cmd.Start()` and discarded the `*exec.Cmd`. `Setsid` detaches the controlling terminal but does **not** reparent the child, so the daemon stayed a child of the long-lived `plumb serve` that spawned it; with no `Wait()`, a `SIGTERM` from `restart`/`stop` left an unreaped zombie. Because `stopByPID`'s liveness check is `kill -0` (which succeeds for a zombie still in the process table), the stop loop then polled for the full 5 s and mis-reported the daemon as "may still be running". Fix: after a successful `Start()`, `startDaemonProcess` now closes the spawner's copy of the log fd (a pre-existing leak) and reaps the child in a background goroutine (new `reapAfterExit` helper) ‚Äî so the zombie is reaped within milliseconds of exit and the stop loop sees it gone. The short-lived `restart`/`stop` callers were never the problem (their spawned daemon reparents to init and is reaped there); it was always the long-lived `serve`. Guard: `TestReapAfterExit`.

### Changed
- **The TUI Settings screen no longer mislabels live-reloadable settings as needing a daemon restart.** Every persisted Settings change already pushes `reload-config` to the daemon (`afterSettingChange` ‚Üí `applyConfigReloadLive`), which hot-reloads edits/git/topology into running sessions ‚Äî yet 13 of 16 rows were hardcoded `restart: true` and the status line always said "applies on next daemon start". The two `live`/`restart` bools on `settingItem` are replaced by a single `reloadTier` (`reloadLive` / `reloadNextSession` / `reloadRestart`), computed from one source of truth, `reloadTierFor` (`internal/tui/model_settings.go`), which mirrors `config.RestartSensitiveEqual`: **only log format + cache** truly need a restart; edits (strict, show-write-diff, rate limit), git policy, and topology apply **live** to running sessions; quality, `auto_attach`, and `lsp_query` timeout apply on the **next session/attach**. Rows now render `live` / `next session` / `*`, the status line wording matches the tier, and the legend explains both markers. Guards: `TestReloadTierFor` (anti-drift, pinned to the `RestartSensitiveEqual` set), `TestSettingsToggle_PersistsAndMarksLive`, `TestSettingsLogFormat_StatusMarksRestart`.
- **`session_start` tells an honest LSP story instead of claiming "LSP is available" whenever a language is detected.** The "Recommended first step" branch gated on `t.diag != nil`, but the diagnostics source is wired for *every* session regardless of whether a language server attached ‚Äî so a Java/Maven project (jdtls is opt-in, off by default) was told to use `workspace_symbols` while the LSP tools returned nothing. session_start now consults the **actually attached** LSP language (new `connSession.acquiredLanguageName()` wired via `SessionStart.WithLSPLanguage`, returning `""` for `LanguageNone`): it advertises LSP only when a server is attached, else points at the topology index when active, else (a recognised project with neither) names the concrete next step ‚Äî for an opt-in adapter, `[lsp.<key>] enabled = true` plus "ensure the server is on PATH"; for the on-by-default Go/Python adapters, "the binary likely isn't installed"; for languages plumb has no server for, `search_in_files`/topology. `detectLanguage` was generalised to `detectLanguageInfo` (label + canonical LSP key). Guards: new "language detected but no LSP attached names the knob" case + updated LSP-available cases in `session_start_test.go`.
- **Topology indexing is now ON by default** (`internal/config/config.go`: `Topology.Enabled` `false` ‚Üí `true`). Out of the box, `topology_*`, ranked search, `file_outline`, and the LSP‚Üítopology fallback work without any config; previously they were silent until a user discovered `[topology] enabled = true`. **Behaviour change to note:** on first attach to a workspace plumb now creates `<workspace>/.plumb/topology.db` (and a `.plumb/.gitignore` excluding it) ‚Äî this is the one case where plumb materialises `.plumb/` for a project that did not have it. Opt out per-project or globally with `[topology] enabled = false`; an explicit `false` always wins, so no "unset vs false" tri-state was needed. This is a **blanket** default-on (a deliberate user decision) rather than the scoped/auto approach previously sketched in `docs/internal/todo.md`; the remaining open item there is now just that per-project `[topology]` *tuning* (not enable/disable) is still ignored by the pool. Docs updated: `AGENTS.md`, `docs/topology.md`, `docs/configuration.md`. Default-asserting tests flipped (`TestDefaults_TopologyEnabledAndMaxFileSize`, `TestCheckTopology_DisabledByConfig`).

## 0.8.4 (2026-05-26)

### Changed
- **`make verify` now compiles and vets the `//go:build integration` files** via a new `build-integration` target (`go vet -tags=integration ./...`); `verify` is now `build test lint build-integration`. `test`/`lint` run *without* the build tag, so integration-only files were never compiled or linted locally ‚Äî the gap that let 0.8.1 (`cbd3cd6`) commit a `cmd/smoke` that did not build under `-tags=integration` from a clean checkout (the `harness_test.go` helper was never `git add`ed; restored in `3be7a62`). CI already ran an `integration` job (`.github/workflows/ci.yml`), so this aligns the local "ready to commit" gate with CI instead of relying on the push to catch it.

## 0.8.3 (2026-05-26)

### Added
- **`read_file` accepts Claude Code's native read window ‚Äî `offset` + `limit`.** `read_file` gained real `offset` (first line) and `limit` (line count) integer parameters ‚Äî the exact window Claude Code's native Read uses ‚Äî alongside plumb's `start_line`/`end_line` (`offset` is a synonym for `start_line`; `limit` and `end_line` are mutually exclusive). They are *declared* params, not mere aliases: an MCP client serialises a parameter absent from the tool's schema as a string, which a key-rename alias cannot coerce back to an integer (verified live ‚Äî `offset` arrived as `"15"`), so a typed declared param is the robust fix. `resolveLineWindow` (`internal/tools/read_file.go`) reconciles the two windows; guard `TestReadFile_Limit`.

### Changed
- **Every `uri`-taking tool now accepts a plain absolute path as readily as a `file://` URI ‚Äî consistency with the filesystem tools.** Previously only the filesystem tools (`read_file`, `list_directory`, ‚Ä¶) documented "path or `file://` URI"; the LSP query/edit tools (`diagnostics`, `get_definition`, `find_references`, `find_symbol`, `list_symbols`, `file_outline`, `explain_symbol`, `call_hierarchy`, `type_hierarchy`, `rename_symbol`, and the four symbol-edit tools) required a `file://` URI and silently returned nothing when handed a plain path. A shared `toFileURI` normaliser (`internal/tools/uri.go`, generalising read_symbol's `resolveReadSymbolPaths`) is applied at each tool's entry, and the alias engine now maps `path`/`file_path ‚Üí uri` so a wrong-but-meaningful key resolves too. Relative paths remain unsupported on `uri` tools (the language server needs an absolute URI). Also added the `symbol ‚Üí name` alias (for `read_symbol`). The reason this was split (filesystem tools took paths; LSP tools mirrored the protocol's `file://`-only `uri`) is documented in `docs/tools.md` ‚Äî it was a naming convention, not a constraint. Guards: `TestToFileURI`, `TestDiagnostics_PlainPath`, and new `TestResolveArgs` cases.

## 0.8.2 (2026-05-26)

### Added
- **`session_start` now reports the live, resolved git tool policy, so an agent never has to guess (or trust a stale memory about) whether it can commit through plumb.** The orientation packet gained a "## Git (via the `git` tool ‚Äî live policy)" section: when `[git] allow_writes` is on it states commits & staging are enabled and steers the agent to commit through the `git` tool rather than the shell, alongside the destructive/push gate states and protected branches; when writes are off it says read-only and names the knob (`[git] allow_writes = false`). Every variant closes with "trust it over any cached note" ‚Äî that line exists to contradict a stale "plumb:git is read-only" assumption at the point of orientation, which is the exact failure that prompted this (an agent shelled out for commits even though `allow_writes` defaults to **true**). The reported policy is the same live, hot-reloaded value the `git` tool gates on: the inline `tools.GitPolicy` closure in `internal/cli/conn.go` was extracted into a shared `connSession.gitPolicy()` method now passed to both `NewGit` and `NewSessionStart`. The section is nil-safe (omitted when unwired) and only emitted inside a git repository. New pure formatter `formatGitPolicy` + `writeSessionGitPolicy` (`internal/tools/session_start.go`); guards `TestFormatGitPolicy` and `TestSessionStart_GitPolicySection`.

## 0.8.1 (2026-05-25)

### Added
- **`selftest` MCP prompt ‚Äî an agent-driven self-test of every tool against a disposable sandbox.** A fourth built-in prompt (`internal/mcp/selftest_prompt.go`, registered in `internal/cli/conn.go` beside `orient`/`whats-broken`/`recent-changes`). `Expand()` returns a deterministic playbook the agent runs against the **live** workspace: a sandbox protocol (a throwaway `selftest-sandbox/` for filesystem ops; a disposable in-module scratch source file for the LSP symbol-edit tools, because the language server only indexes files inside the module; SKIP on languages with no LSP), an ordered Tier A‚ÜíC checklist (read-only queries ‚Üí filesystem writes confined to files it just created ‚Üí symbol edits in the scratch file), mandatory cleanup, and a PASS/FAIL/SKIP report. This is the real-world complement to the `cmd/smoke` wire-level test ‚Äî the actual agent drives the actual tools, so it surfaces confusing descriptions or awkward parameters a Go test cannot. Cold-start, diagnostics-timing, and dirty-guard footguns are baked into the playbook; tools that are unsafe or non-deterministic to run live (git_init, destructive/network git, transaction rollback, strict-mode, rate-limit) are explicitly deferred to the integration harness.
- **Anti-rot coverage guard, in two halves.** `TestSelftestPrompt_CoversEveryTool` (`internal/mcp/selftest_prompt_test.go`) asserts every tool in the canonical coverage list (`SelftestToolNames`) is named verbatim in the playbook; `TestSmoke_ToolListParity` (`cmd/smoke/tierd_test.go`, integration) asserts that canonical list equals the live `tools/list`. Together a tool added without a checklist entry ‚Äî or a stale entry left behind ‚Äî fails CI.
- **`cmd/smoke` Tier-D coverage (`cmd/smoke/tierd_test.go`, integration).** The behaviours the agent self-test defers, driven against a bare language-less fixture (no gopls, instant attach): `TestSmoke_StrictModeRejectsUnreadEdit` (strict mode blocks an unread `edit_file`, then a `read_file` opens the gate), `TestSmoke_TransactionRollback` (an unmatchable op leaves the first file untouched ‚Äî all-or-nothing), and `TestSmoke_GitTiers` (`git_init` ‚Üí `add`/`commit` write-tier ‚Üí `reset --hard` destructive-tier gated by `PLUMB_GIT_ALLOW_DESTRUCTIVE` + `confirm`). `isolatedEnv`/`newMCPClient` gained an `extraEnv` variadic so each test spawns a daemon with its own config.
- **End-to-end reconnect coverage for the 0.8.0 resilient proxy (`cmd/smoke/reconnect_test.go`, integration).** `TestSmoke_ProxyReconnect` drives a real `plumb serve` over the MCP wire, kills the daemon mid-session (`plumb stop --force`), then asserts a fresh `version`/`daemon_info` call still succeeds and the daemon PID changed ‚Äî proving at the wire level (not just the unit level of `internal/cli/serve_proxy_test.go`) that the proxy dial-or-spawned a new daemon and replayed the handshake transparently. The shared `cmd/smoke` harness (MCP client, fixture builder, assertion helpers) was extracted into `cmd/smoke/harness_test.go` and `isolatedEnv` was tightened to isolate `XDG_CONFIG_HOME` too; the original wire-level happy path was restored as `TestSmoke_EndToEnd` on top of the shared harness.

## 0.8.0 (2026-05-25)

### Added
- **`plumb serve` survives a daemon crash or hang without the client noticing.** The proxy was a raw byte pump (`proxyStdio`, two `io.Copy` goroutines): when the daemon died the copy returned EOF and the `serve` process exited, killing the client's MCP server and forcing a manual reconnect. The new `reconnectingProxy` (`internal/cli/serve_proxy.go` + `serve_proxy_frame.go`) keeps the client's stdio open across a daemon failure, transparently re-establishes the daemon (dial-or-spawn via the existing `connectOrStartDaemon`), and **replays the captured MCP handshake** on the client's behalf ‚Äî the client sends `initialize` exactly once and never re-sends it, so the proxy stashes the raw `initialize`/`notifications/initialized` frames and resends them to the fresh daemon, swallowing the replayed `initialize` response (the client already has one). It tracks in-flight request ids (normalised via `idKey`) and, after reconnecting, writes a synthesised retryable JSON-RPC error (`code -32000`) for each, so a tool call interrupted by the crash returns one error the agent retries rather than hanging forever. Non-idempotent writes are never auto-replayed. Bounded reconnect retries with exponential backoff; on give-up the proxy exits with a clear message, restoring the legacy behaviour rather than spinning forever on a crash-looping daemon. "Good enough" transparency: the session survives a brief pause and per-session daemon state (read-tracking, caches) is rebuilt, not preserved. Guards: `TestProxyCrashRecovery`, `TestProxyGivesUpAfterMaxReconnects`, `TestIDKeyNormalisation`, `TestEnvelopeClassification` (`internal/cli/serve_proxy_test.go`), all green under `-race`.
- **Hang detection via heartbeat (`internal/cli/serve_proxy_heartbeat.go`).** A crashed daemon is caught by the pumps' I/O errors; a *hung* daemon (alive but unresponsive) is caught by an idle `ping` probe on a reserved id namespace (`__plumb_hb_*`), whose pong the proxy consumes. Because the MCP server dispatches every message concurrently (`internal/mcp/server.go` `Serve`), a live daemon answers `ping` even mid-tool-call, so a missed pong within the timeout ‚Äî with no other daemon traffic meanwhile ‚Äî is a real hang signal, not a busy daemon. On detection the proxy kills the stuck daemon (`SIGTERM`‚Üí`SIGKILL` via the PID file, reusing `readDaemonPID`/`processAlive`) and runs the ordinary reconnect path, which spawns a fresh one. Guard: `TestProxyHangDetection`.
- **Config: `PLUMB_PROXY_RECONNECT` (default on; `0`/`false`/`off` reverts to the legacy byte-pump proxy), `PLUMB_PROXY_HEARTBEAT` (Go duration; `0` disables hang detection while keeping crash recovery), and a `--no-reconnect` flag on `plumb serve`.** `internal/cli/serve.go`.
- **`plumb restart`** ‚Äî stops the daemon and immediately brings a fresh one back up (`internal/cli/restart.go`). It follows the same rules as `plumb stop`: it renders active sessions and asks to confirm before proceeding, with `--force` to skip. The stop-confirmation gate was generalised (`daemonActionPrompt`, `confirmDaemonActionWithActiveSessions`) so both commands share it with action-appropriate wording. Paired with the resilient proxy, a restart is transparent to connected clients ‚Äî their `plumb serve` reconnects to the new daemon automatically ‚Äî so it does not take longer than a stop and no conversation has to re-establish its session. `respawnDaemon` first checks whether a resilient client already respawned the daemon, otherwise spawns one under the shared `plumb.spawn.lock`. Guards: `TestRestartActionPromptWording`, `TestDialDaemonOnce` (`internal/cli/restart_test.go`).

### Changed
- **The daemon-architecture docs no longer describe `plumb serve` as byte-dumb.** `AGENTS.md` updated to document the resilient proxy and the two new env knobs.

## 0.7.29 (2026-05-25)

### Fixed
- **Dashboard "Top Tools" panels now share one frame height side by side.** When the daemon has just started, the *Top Tools (uptime)* table has far fewer rows than *Top Tools (all time)*, so its content-driven box was shorter; `joinWidgetRow` then padded the gap with unbordered whitespace, leaving the uptime frame closing partway down with a borderless void beneath it. A new pure helper `padBoxHeight` (`internal/tui/dashboard.go`) grows the shorter `dashBox` to the taller box's height by inserting blank **bordered** rows just above its bottom border (reusing the box's own padding line, so width and style match). Applied in the side-by-side branch of `dashTopToolsTables` (`internal/tui/dashboard_widgets.go`); the stacked layout and the generic `joinWidgetRow` are untouched. Guard: `TestDashTopToolsTablesEqualFrameHeightSideBySide`.

## 0.7.28 (2026-05-25)

### Added
- **Live configuration store with auto change detection ‚Äî the global config now reloads without a daemon restart.** A daemon-singleton `config.Store` (`internal/config/store.go`) holds the global base config behind an `atomic.Pointer[Config]` (lock-free `Current()`), with a monotonic generation counter, a last-reloaded timestamp, and a `Subscribe`/notify observer API (notifications fire outside the lock so a listener may re-enter the store). Three inputs drive `store.Reload`: (1) an **fsnotify directory watcher** on the global-config directory (`internal/cli/config_global_watcher.go`) that reloads on external edits (vim, etc.), debounced 250 ms, watching the *directory* not the file so it survives the atomic-rename swap; (2) a new **`reload-config` control-socket command** (`internal/cli/log_level.go`); (3) the **TUI**, which pushes `reload-config` after saving any setting (`internal/tui/model_settings_keys.go`). Each MCP session subscribes and re-merges its per-project view on a global change (`internal/cli/conn.go`), so `[edits]`/`[git]`/`[walk]`/rate-limit apply live to every active session. `connSession.cfg` (a by-value snapshot) became `*config.Store`; `applyProjectConfig` is now serialised by `applyMu` and merges against the live global base. Guards: `internal/config/store_test.go`, `TestApplyProjectConfig_UsesLiveGlobalBase`, `TestGlobalConfigChange_ReappliesSession`, `TestShouldReload`, `TestGlobalConfigWatcher_ReloadsOnFileChange` (integration).
- **`plumb config reload`** ‚Äî a CLI sibling of `plumb log-level` that forces an immediate global-config reload over the control socket (`internal/cli/config.go`). The control-socket round-trip is now shared via `dialDaemonCtrl`.
- **Live topology reconciliation.** `topologyPool.Reconcile` (`internal/cli/topology_pool.go`) applies global `[topology]` changes live: disabling closes open stores; a tuning change re-opens them with the new config; an unchanged config is a no-op (cheap across unrelated edits). Closes the long-standing "per-project topology config only toggles enable/disable" gap for the global layer. Safe because the indexer is a background subsystem with no synchronous request path. Guards: `internal/cli/topology_pool_test.go`.
- **Restart-needed signalling for settings the daemon cannot reload live.** `Store.RestartNeeded()` compares the live config's restart-bound subset ‚Äî LSP server definitions, cache sizing, and log format (`config.RestartSensitiveEqual`) ‚Äî against the daemon's startup config. Surfaced three ways: a daemon WARN on the offending reload; a `restart needed:` line in the **`daemon_info`** tool (which now also reports `config generation` and `config reloaded`, via a nil-safe `WithConfigStatus`); and a **Reload behaviour** legend in **`plumb config show`**. Guards: `internal/tools/daemon_info_test.go`, `TestStore_RestartNeeded`, `TestRestartSensitiveEqual`.
- **Atomic `config.Save`.** `config.Save` now stages the encoded TOML in a dotfile-prefixed temp file and renames it over the target (`internal/config/config.go`), so a reader or the file watcher never sees a half-written config and a crash mid-write leaves the previous file intact; existing file permissions are preserved. The dotfile prefix keeps the watcher from reacting to staging writes. Guard: `TestSave_AtomicLeavesNoTempFiles`.

### Changed
- **Global config is no longer "loaded once at daemon start".** It lives in the `config.Store` and is re-read on file change / control-socket request / TUI push. `AGENTS.md` and `docs/configuration.md` updated.
- **Moved `docs/feedbacks.md` ‚Üí `internal/feedbacks.md`** (references updated in `docs/internal/autonomous-loop.md` and `docs/internal/todo.md`).

### Notes
- **LSP-process config (`lsp.<lang>` command/args/env/markers) and `cache`/`log_format` remain restart-bound by design.** Live LSP-server reload was investigated and deferred: the routing proxy re-acquires per request (URI-bearing methods would migrate), but `setPrimary` pins a `*clientProxy` per session, so a reliable live swap needs session-level re-attachment + reference counting, or a routing-proxy refactor with grace-period draining ‚Äî too large/risky to ship without integration tests against a live server. The restart-signal is the reliable interim. Full design and routing-model analysis recorded in `docs/internal/todo-to-review.md`.
- **New dependency:** `github.com/fsnotify/fsnotify` v1.10.1 (pure-Go, no CGo).

## 0.7.27 (2026-05-25)

### Changed
- **The dirty-guard is now session-aware ‚Äî re-editing a file plumb wrote this session is never blocked.** Previously every write tool refused a dirty target unless `dirty_ok: true` was set, which fired on the *second* edit of any file during normal iteration (the first edit makes the file dirty). A new per-session `WriteTracker` (`internal/tools/write_tracker.go`, one per MCP connection, mirroring `ReadTracker`) records every path plumb writes; the guard (`dirtyBlocksWrite` / `dirtyBlocksMove`, `internal/tools/file_write_helpers.go`) now blocks only when a file is dirty **and** plumb did not write it this session. So iterating on plumb-touched files never nags, while a file left dirty *before* plumb touched it (uncommitted work plumb did not create) still requires `dirty_ok` ‚Äî the one case the guard exists to protect. Wired into `write_file`, `edit_file`, `delete_file`, `find_replace`, `rename_file`, `copy_file`, and `transaction_apply` via the new `WriteDeps.Writes` field. Guards: `TestWriteTracker_RecordWrote`/`_NilSafe`, `TestDirtyBlocksWrite_SessionAware`, `TestDirtyBlocksMove_SessionAware`, `TestEditFile_SessionAwareDirtyGuard`, `TestEditFile_DirtyGuardBlocksPreExistingDirt`.

## 0.7.26 (2026-05-25)

### Fixed
- **Post-write diagnostics are no longer stale.** `edit_file` and `write_file` previously returned the pre-write error snapshot because `awaitDiagnosticsRefresh` polled `WaitDiagnostics`, which returns immediately when diagnostics for the URI are already tracked (always true after the first publication). The wait is now signal-based: a new `WaitNextDiagnostics(ctx, uri)` method on `Invalidator` subscribes a channel before returning, so it always waits for the *next* `publishDiagnostics` notification ‚Äî never the cached one. `awaitDiagnosticsRefresh` rewritten to use `context.WithTimeout` + `WaitNextDiagnostics`; the `baseline []protocol.Diagnostic` parameter removed. `internal/cache/invalidator.go`, `internal/cli/routing_proxy.go`, `internal/tools/file_write_helpers.go`, `internal/tools/edit_file.go`, `internal/tools/write_file.go`.
- **`edit_file` / `write_file` no longer hang silently when gopls is saturated.** `conn.Notify` (`internal/lsp/jsonrpc/conn.go`) called `c.send` synchronously while holding the write mutex, so a saturated gopls stdin pipe (e.g. after writing a 52 KB file that triggered a multi-minute analysis) blocked the entire MCP tool call indefinitely. `send` is now launched in a goroutine; `Notify` selects on the result, `ctx.Done()`, and connection close ‚Äî the call returns promptly while the write completes in the background. Guards: `TestConn_Notify_SendsMessage`, `TestConn_Notify_ContextCancelUnblocks` (`internal/lsp/jsonrpc/conn_test.go`).
- **`git add` now stages tracked deletions.** `buildGitArgv` produced `["add", "--"] + files`; `git add -- <path>` refuses a pathspec that no longer exists on disk, so staging a deletion failed with `fatal: pathspec did not match any files`. Changed to `["add", "-A", "--"] + files` ‚Äî new, modified, and deleted entries are all staged. Behaviour for existing files is unchanged. `internal/tools/git.go`; guard `TestGit_AddStagesTrackedDeletion`.
- **`git rm` now returns an actionable hint instead of a generic rejection.** The error now reads: `git: subcommand "rm" is not permitted; to remove a tracked file, use delete_file to remove it from disk, then stage the deletion with git add`. `internal/tools/git.go`; guard `TestGit_RmRejectedWithDeleteFileHint`.
- **`rename_file` / `copy_file` no longer require `dirty_ok` for untracked source files.** `dirtyBasenamesInDir` parsed `??`-prefixed lines from `git status --porcelain` (untracked files) as dirty, blocking a move/copy unless `dirty_ok: true` was set. A move/copy preserves the source content, so an untracked source has nothing at HEAD to lose ‚Äî the new `pathIsDirtyIgnoringUntracked` variant skips `??` lines for `rename_file` and `copy_file` only. The destructive tools (`write_file`, `edit_file`, `delete_file`, `find_replace`, `transaction_apply`) keep treating an untracked file as dirty, since overwriting or deleting one destroys content git cannot recover. `internal/tools/file_write_helpers.go`; guards `TestPathIsDirty_UntrackedFile`, `TestPathIsDirtyIgnoringUntracked_ModifiedTrackedFile`.
- **`session_start` now returns a clear error when the explicit `workspace` arg differs from the already-attached workspace.** Previously the arg was silently ignored and the response kept showing the original workspace, giving the agent a confident but wrong workspace. The error now reads: `session_start: workspace is already pinned to /path/old ‚Äî cannot re-pin to /path/new in the same connection. To switch projects, start a new MCP connection.` If the explicit arg matches the attached workspace, behaviour is unchanged. `internal/tools/session_start.go`.
- **Unknown-parameter errors now include the tool name.** `unknownErr` (`internal/mcp/argguard.go`) now prefixes its message with the tool name (e.g. `write_file: unknown parameter "workspace" ‚Ä¶`), making it clear which tool's schema was consulted when an agent confuses two tools. The name is threaded from `resolveToolArgs` through `resolveArgs`, `validateObject`, and `validateChild`. `internal/mcp/argguard.go`, `internal/mcp/server.go`; guard `TestResolveArgs_ToolNamePrefix`.

### Changed
- **`git` tool schema descriptions clarified.** The `args`, `files`, and `message` field descriptions now explicitly state which subcommands each applies to; `Description()` summarises the typed-parameter contract. `internal/tools/git.go`.

### Docs
- **`post_write_diagnostics_ms` documented in `AGENTS.md`.** The `[edits]` configuration table was missing this entry despite the config field, env-var binding (`PLUMB_POST_WRITE_DIAG_MS`), and wiring all existing. `AGENTS.md`.

## 0.7.25 (2026-05-25)

### Fixed
- **LSP `command` paths in config now expand `~/` and `$VAR` references.** The daemon is a background singleton that inherits a minimal PATH from its launcher (Claude Desktop, a LaunchAgent, etc.), so bare binary names like `gopls` fail with `executable file not found in $PATH` even when the binary is installed at `~/go/bin/gopls`. `normaliseConfig` now runs `expandPath` on every `LSPConfig.Command` after each config layer loads: `~/go/bin/gopls` expands to the user's real home directory via `os.UserHomeDir()`, and `$GOPATH/bin/gopls` or `$HOME/go/bin/gopls` expand via `os.ExpandEnv`. Bare names (e.g. the default `gopls`) and absolute paths are unchanged. `internal/config/config.go`; guards `TestExpandPath` and `TestNormaliseConfig_LSPCommandExpanded`.

## 0.7.24 (2026-05-25)

### Fixed
- **The argument guard now rejects unknown *nested* keys, not just top-level ones.** The dispatch-path guard (`internal/mcp/argguard.go`, 0.7.19) already recurses validation into nested object / array-of-object levels, but `edit_file`'s `edits[]` items and `transaction_apply`'s operation object + `edits[]` items did not declare `"additionalProperties": false`, so a stray nested key (e.g. a typo'd field in an edit) was silently dropped instead of caught. Adding the marker to every nested object level of the two schemas (`internal/tools/edit_file.go`, `internal/tools/transaction.go` ‚Äî the only two tools with nested object schemas) closes the gap: an unknown nested key now gets the same teaching rejection as a top-level one (`unknown parameter "edits[].foo"; valid parameters: old_string, new_string`), while recognised aliases (`old_str`‚Üí`old_string`) are still rewritten first. Every legitimate nested field is declared, so nothing valid is rejected. **Behaviour change:** extra nested keys previously dropped silently are now rejected ‚Äî strictly better and consistent with the top-level contract. Guards: a nested-rejection case in `TestResolveArgs` (`internal/mcp/argguard_test.go`) and `TestNestedSchemasRejectUnknownProperties` (`internal/tools/schema_contract_test.go`), which walks the assembled schemas so a removed nested marker fails loudly.

## 0.7.23 (2026-05-25)

### Fixed
- **The `$HOME` guard in workspace detection now compares by filesystem identity, not by string.** The `.git/` root-marker guard added in 0.7.20 excludes `$HOME` (so a dotfiles repo there cannot turn the whole home directory into a workspace) ‚Äî but it did so with a raw `dir != home` string compare on an un-normalised path, defeatable by a trailing slash (`/Users/you/`) or a symlink/firmlink spelling of `$HOME`, either of which would have resolved all of `$HOME` as a workspace, the exact outcome the guard exists to prevent. `Detect` (`internal/cli/pool.go`) now `filepath.Clean`s the start path and compares against a once-stat'd `$HOME` via `os.SameFile` (new `sameDirAs` helper) ‚Äî robust to trailing slashes, `.`/`..` segments, symlinks, and macOS firmlinks ‚Äî and falls inert (never refusing a legitimate repo) when `$HOME` is undeterminable or the directory cannot be stat'd. Surfaced reviewing the 0.7.20 workspace-resolution change. Regression guards: `TestDetect_GitAtHomeTrailingSlashRefused`, `TestDetect_GitAtHomeViaSymlinkRefused` (`internal/cli/pool_test.go`).

## 0.7.22 (2026-05-24)

### Fixed
- **`read_multiple_files` no longer fails every file with `read_file: file_path is required`.** It reads each file by calling `read_file` **in-process** (`internal/tools/read_multiple_files.go`), a path that does not cross the MCP dispatch boundary where the parameter-alias engine runs ‚Äî and that internal call was still passing the pre-0.7.19 key `path`, stranded once `read_file`'s canonical key became `file_path`. The internal call now uses the canonical `file_path`. The alias engine itself was never broken: it rewrites a *client's* `path`‚Üí`file_path` with a warning at dispatch, as designed and tested. This was plumb's own internal caller carrying a stale key, and `read_multiple_files` is the only in-process tool‚Üítool call in the codebase (every other `"path"` is a log field or a tool where `path` is genuinely canonical). New `internal/tools/read_multiple_files_test.go` drives the real `read_multiple_files`‚Üí`read_file` path (the tool had no test before, which is why the rename slipped through), and two `TestResolveArgs` cases (`internal/mcp/argguard_test.go`) confirm the alias is bidirectional and schema-aware ‚Äî `path`‚Üí`file_path` for `read_file`-style tools and `file_path`‚Üí`path` for `path`-canonical tools like `read_symbol` ‚Äî each accepted with a warning.

## 0.7.21 (2026-05-24)

### Fixed
- **The dashboard's "uptime" widgets now track the real daemon uptime instead of the oldest live session.** The TUI Dashboard's "Tokens Saved (uptime)", "Top Tools (uptime)", and the activity chart's "‚Üë N calls (uptime)" were all anchored on `m.sessions[0].StartedAt` ‚Äî the earliest *currently-connected* session (`session.List()` prunes dead-PID files) ‚Äî with a `now ‚àí 1 minute` fallback. Because conversations start and end while the daemon keeps running, the "uptime" window actually tracked "age of the oldest live conversation", not the daemon: a 6-hour-old daemon whose only live conversation began 3 minutes ago showed a 3-minute uptime and scoped every uptime-labelled stat to those 3 minutes; a conversation ending and a new one starting made the window jump; with no live sessions it fell back to an arbitrary last minute. The fix exposes the daemon's real start time (`daemonStartedAt`, already captured at boot and reported by `daemon_info`) to the TUI by adding `StartedAt` to the metrics snapshot the TUI already polls every 2s (`monitor.DaemonMetrics` + `StartSnapshotWriter`, `internal/monitor/metrics.go`; threaded from `internal/cli/daemon.go`). A single shared anchor ‚Äî `dashboardUptimeStart` (`internal/tui/dashboard.go`), now also used by `refreshActivity` (`internal/tui/model_refresh.go`) ‚Äî returns that daemon start time when the snapshot is fresh, falling back to the previous oldest-live-session ‚Üí `now‚àí1m` logic when it is not (so the TUI degrades gracefully against a stale/absent snapshot or an old daemon build that does not publish the field). No stats-schema change: the daemon-singleton `flock` guarantees every recorded call since `daemonStartedAt` belongs to the current run, so the existing time-windowed queries become exact. Guards: `TestDashboardUptimeStart` (`internal/tui/model_test.go`) and the `StartedAt` round-trip in `TestSnapshotRoundTrip` (`internal/monitor/metrics_test.go`).

## 0.7.20 (2026-05-24)

### Fixed
- **Sessions in a git repo with no language marker no longer hang on "resolving‚Ä¶".** `workspacePool.Detect` (`internal/cli/pool.go`) now recognises a `.git/` directory as a lowest-priority workspace root marker, returning `(root, LanguageNone)`. Previously `Detect` knew only `.plumb/` and language root markers (`go.mod`, `pyproject.toml`, ‚Ä¶); a scripts / multi-language repo (e.g. a PowerShell + Python runbook tree under a git root) matched none of them, so `Detect` errored on every path-bearing tool call and ‚Äî with `auto_attach` off by default ‚Äî the session never attached. Symptom: the TUI showed `Folder: (resolving workspace‚Ä¶)` indefinitely with `Tools: 0 / Calls: 0` (no workspace root ‚áí `onAfterTool` recorded nothing), even while the client was actively using tools. The `.git/` marker closes the gap in the default config (no `auto_attach` needed); precedence is per-directory nearest-wins, so a `.plumb/` or language marker still beats an ancestor `.git/`, and `$HOME` is excluded so a dotfiles repo there cannot capture the whole home directory. The pre-existing `auto_attach`/`SynthesiseRoot` path still covers the residual case of a seed dir with no `.git/` anywhere above it. Regression guards: `TestDetect_GitDirOnly`, `TestDetect_GitDirInAncestor`, `TestDetect_LanguageMarkerWinsOverGit`, `TestDetect_NearestLanguageMarkerWinsOverAncestorGit`, `TestDetect_GitAtHomeRefused` (`internal/cli/pool_test.go`).
- **TUI now renders an undetectable language as `?` instead of nothing.** A `LanguageNone` session (valid workspace, no LSP language ‚Äî it still serves language-independent calls) shows a `?` badge in the Sessions list and `Language ?` in the details panel (`sessionLangLabel`, `internal/tui/model_left.go`; details row in `model_right.go`), making clear the session is attached and usable rather than stuck.
- **`session_start` no longer reports a phantom workspace from the daemon's working directory.** Its resolution chain dropped the `os.Getwd()` walk-up fallback (`coldStartWorkspace`): the daemon is a singleton shared across all connections, so its cwd is never a per-session signal ‚Äî yet for an unresolved session `session_start` would walk up from it and confidently report an unrelated directory (e.g. the plumb checkout the daemon was launched from) that it never actually attached, so the agent saw one workspace while the TUI showed "resolving‚Ä¶". The chain is now: the daemon's **attached root (authoritative)** ‚Üí explicit `workspace` arg ‚Üí client `roots/list` ‚Üí honest "pass `workspace`" error. The attached root is now preferred over the explicit arg too, so the displayed workspace always matches what the TUI, memory, and topology use (previously a `workspace` arg pointing at a subdirectory was shown while the daemon had attached the git root). `internal/tools/session_start.go`; guards `TestSessionStart_WorkspaceResolution`.
- **Claude Desktop now gets its tool guidance (and a workspace-pinning instruction).** `isClaudeDesktop` only matched the client name `claude-desktop`, but Claude Desktop identifies over MCP as **`claude-ai`** ‚Äî so `writeClaudeDesktopGuidance` was dead code and Desktop users got no guidance. It now matches `claude-ai` too, and the guidance leads with: plumb cannot detect your folder (Desktop does not report it, the daemon is shared) ‚Äî pass an explicit `workspace` to `session_start` to pin the project. `internal/tools/session_start.go`; guard `TestSessionStart_DesktopGuidance`.

## 0.7.19 (2026-05-24)

### Added
- **TypeScript (`.ts`) topology extraction moved onto tree-sitter ‚Äî the lex-states gap is closed without a fork.** gotreesitter v0.19.1 ships the TypeScript external *scanner* but not the external *lex-states* table (`ts_external_scanner_states`), so typed arrow params (`(u: User): T => ‚Ä¶`) cascaded ERROR nodes (see `docs/internal/treesitter-plan.md`). The fix: the missing `typescriptExternalLexStates` table was regenerated from upstream `tree-sitter-typescript`'s `parser.c` at the **exact pinned commit gotreesitter embeds** (`75b3874‚Ä¶`, recorded in `grammars/grammar_updates.json`) via gotreesitter's bundled `ts2go`, and is supplied at runtime through the grammars package's *exported* `RegisterExternalLexStates` ‚Äî **no vendored fork required** (`internal/topology/extractors/treesitter/ts_lex_states.go`). New `treesitter.NewTypeScript` (`.ts`) replaces the regex extractor for TypeScript: it extracts functions (declarations + arrow/function-expression bindings, incl. `export`ed), classes (incl. `abstract`) with methods, interfaces (‚Üí `KindType`) with their method signatures, type aliases and enums (‚Üí `KindType`) with enum members (‚Üí `KindConstant`), top-level const/let/var, ES/`require` imports, namespace (`internal_module`) members, and describe/it/test blocks (‚Üí `KindTest`); containment 1.0/extractor, intra-file calls 0.8/heuristic. The previously-cascading typed-arrow utility-module layout now parses with **0 ERROR/0 MISSING** (`TestTypeScript_TypedArrowNoCascade` is the regression guard; if a future gotreesitter bump desyncs the table it fails loudly). The `typescript` `langsupport` row flips `EngineRegex ‚Üí EngineTreeSitter` (extensions narrowed to `.ts`).

- **Tool parameter names now match Claude Code's native tools, and a dispatch-path alias layer accepts other agents' names ‚Äî so a wrong-but-meaningful parameter no longer costs extra calls.** Two parts. **(1) Canonical rename:** the file-content tools adopt Claude Code's native parameter names ‚Äî `read_file`/`write_file`/`edit_file`/`delete_file`/`transaction_apply` take `file_path` (was `path`), and `edit_file`/`transaction_apply` edits take `old_string`/`new_string` (was `old_str`/`new_str`). Search/dir tools keep `path`/`pattern` (already matching `Glob`/`Grep`/`LS`). A Claude agent now hits an exact match ‚Äî no alias, no warning. **(2) Alias engine** (`internal/mcp/argguard.go` + `argalias.go`, wired into `handleToolsCall`): before `Execute`, each `tools/call`'s arguments are validated against the tool's declared schema and recognised aliases are rewritten to the canonical name ‚Äî recursively, schema-guided, so nested keys like `edits[].old_str` are fixed too. Resolution is a curated table (`path‚Üífile_path`, `old_str‚Üíold_string`, `filename/file‚Üífile_path`, `dir/directory‚Üípath`, `regex/query‚Üípattern`, `new_name‚Üíname`, ‚Ä¶, applied per-tool only where the canonical is a real parameter and isn't already set) plus case/separator normalisation (`startLine‚Üístart_line`); each applied alias adds a one-line `note:` to the result nudging toward the canonical name. It **never** guesses by edit distance ‚Äî a fuzzy near-match is surfaced only as a "did you mean" *suggestion* in the rejection, never silently applied (safe for write/edit/delete tools). A genuinely unknown parameter, or a missing `required` one, is still rejected with the valid-parameter list. Unknown-property rejection is **opt-in per schema** (`additionalProperties: false`, now on every tool schema, drift-guarded by `TestInputSchemasDeclareAdditionalProperties`); the missing-required check applies regardless; odd/unparseable schemas fail open with a WARN. `rename_session` also gained machine-readable `minLength`/`maxLength`/`pattern` on its `name` argument (pattern agreement with `session.NormaliseName` is test-guarded). Previously a wrong key like `{"new_name": ‚Ä¶}` (or the native `old_string` on `edit_file`) was silently dropped by lenient JSON decoding, producing a misleading `‚Ä¶ is required` and forcing the caller to guess again. `seedPathFromArgs` learned the `file_path` shape so workspace auto-seeding still works.

### Known limitations
- **TSX/JSX (`.tsx`/`.jsx`) stay on the regex extractor.** With the regenerated TSX lex-states attached, JSX itself parses clean, but gotreesitter v0.19.1's **TSX grammar still cascades on typed arrow parameters** (e.g. `const f = (x: number): number => x` ‚Üí 4 ERROR nodes), which would silently drop trailing symbols from typed-arrow-heavy components ‚Äî worse than the regex extractor for real-world `.tsx`. This is a residual grammar issue beyond the lex-states gap. A new `tsx` `langsupport` row (`.tsx`/`.jsx`, `EngineRegex`) keeps them on the narrowed regex extractor; closing it needs an upstream TSX-grammar fix or the WASM/wazero path (tracked in `docs/internal/treesitter-plan.md`). The correct TSX lex-states table is generated and registered (ready for when the grammar issue is resolved).

## 0.7.18 (2026-05-24)

### Added
- **LSP adapter for Kotlin (kotlin-language-server), unit-tested; integration test ready and gated.** New `internal/lsp/adapters/kotlin` implements the full `lsp.Client` interface, answers `client/registerCapability`/`unregisterCapability`, and bases capabilities on `protocol.DefaultClientCapabilities()`. Wired into the daemon (`newAdapter`/`initParamsFor`) and the default `[lsp]` map as `kotlin` (`Command: kotlin-language-server`, `RootMarkers: [settings.gradle.kts, build.gradle.kts]`, **disabled by default** ‚Äî opt in with `[lsp.kotlin] enabled = true`); the `kotlin` `langsupport` row now names `kotlin-language-server`, pairing the semantic GPS with the tree-sitter Kotlin Map. (The `build.gradle.kts` marker overlaps Java's; with both enabled, the alphabetical detect order makes Java win ‚Äî both are opt-in, so this is moot by default.) **Validation status: experimental** ‚Äî unit-tested with the mock transport; the real-binary integration test (`testdata/kotlin-fixture/` + a `DidChangeWatchedFiles` ‚Üí diagnostics round-trip, gated `//go:build integration`) is written but **skips until `kotlin-language-server` is installed** (`brew install kotlin-language-server`). Promote to validated once it has run green against the real server.
- **LSP adapter for TypeScript/JavaScript (typescript-language-server), unit-tested; integration test ready and gated.** New `internal/lsp/adapters/typescript` implements the full `lsp.Client` interface, answers `client/registerCapability`/`unregisterCapability`, and bases capabilities on `protocol.DefaultClientCapabilities()`. Wired into the daemon (`newAdapter`/`initParamsFor`, imported aliased as `tsls` to avoid colliding with the topology `typescript` extractor package) and the default `[lsp]` map as `typescript` (`Command: typescript-language-server`, `Args: [--stdio]`, `RootMarkers: [tsconfig.json, jsconfig.json, package.json]`, **disabled by default** ‚Äî opt in with `[lsp.typescript] enabled = true`). This server serves **both** TypeScript and JavaScript, so both the `typescript` and `javascript` `langsupport` rows now name it ‚Äî pairing the semantic GPS with the regex TS structural Map and the tree-sitter JS Map respectively. **Validation status: experimental** ‚Äî unit-tested with the mock transport; the real-binary integration test (`testdata/typescript-fixture/` + a `DidChangeWatchedFiles` ‚Üí diagnostics round-trip, gated `//go:build integration`) is written but **skips until `typescript-language-server` is installed** (`npm install -g typescript-language-server typescript`). Promote to validated once it has run green against the real server.
- **LSP adapter for Zig (zls), unit-tested; integration test ready and gated.** New `internal/lsp/adapters/zig` implements the full `lsp.Client` interface, answers `client/registerCapability`/`unregisterCapability`, and bases capabilities on `protocol.DefaultClientCapabilities()`. Wired into the daemon (`newAdapter`/`initParamsFor`) and the default `[lsp]` map as `zig` (`Command: zls`, `RootMarkers: [build.zig, build.zig.zon]`, **disabled by default** ‚Äî opt in with `[lsp.zig] enabled = true`); the `zig` `langsupport` row now names `zls`, pairing the semantic GPS with the tree-sitter Zig Map. **Validation status: experimental** ‚Äî unit-tested with the mock transport (every interface method); the real-binary integration test (`testdata/zig-fixture/` + a `DidChangeWatchedFiles` ‚Üí diagnostics round-trip, gated `//go:build integration`) is written but **skips until `zls` is installed on the validation machine** (it was not). Promote to validated once it has run green against a real zls. zls + tree-sitter-zig track the Zig language version (pre-1.0).
- **LSP adapter for Swift (sourcekit-lsp), validated against the real binary.** New `internal/lsp/adapters/swift` implements the full `lsp.Client` interface, answers `client/registerCapability`/`unregisterCapability`, and bases capabilities on `protocol.DefaultClientCapabilities()`. Wired into the daemon (`newAdapter`/`initParamsFor`) and the default `[lsp]` map as `swift` (`Command: sourcekit-lsp`, `RootMarkers: [Package.swift]`, **disabled by default** ‚Äî opt in with `[lsp.swift] enabled = true`); the `swift` `langsupport` row now names `sourcekit-lsp`, pairing the semantic GPS with the tree-sitter Swift Map. sourcekit-lsp ships with the Swift toolchain (Xcode or swift.org; `/usr/bin/sourcekit-lsp` on macOS) and derives per-file compiler arguments from the SwiftPM build plan. Unit-tested with the mock transport and **integration-tested against a real sourcekit-lsp** (gated `//go:build integration`, `testdata/swift-fixture/` SwiftPM package): document-symbol extraction + a `DidChangeWatchedFiles` + `DidOpen` ‚Üí diagnostics round-trip, both passing.
- **LSP adapter for Rust (rust-analyzer), validated against the real binary.** New `internal/lsp/adapters/rust` implements the full `lsp.Client` interface (mirroring the pyright worked example), answers `client/registerCapability`/`unregisterCapability` via `SetRequestHandler` so rust-analyzer's dynamic file-watcher registration is honoured, and bases its client capabilities on `protocol.DefaultClientCapabilities()`. Wired into the daemon (`newAdapter`/`initParamsFor` in `internal/cli/pool.go`) and added to the default `[lsp]` map as `rust` (`Command: rust-analyzer`, `RootMarkers: [Cargo.toml]`, **disabled by default** ‚Äî opt in with `[lsp.rust] enabled = true`); the `rust` `langsupport` row now names `rust-analyzer` as its adapter, pairing the semantic GPS with the existing tree-sitter Rust Map. Unit-tested with the mock transport (every interface method) and **integration-tested against a real rust-analyzer** (gated `//go:build integration`, `testdata/rust-fixture/`): a document-symbol extraction test and a `DidChangeWatchedFiles` + `DidOpen` ‚Üí diagnostics round-trip, both passing. **Cold-start note:** rust-analyzer loads the sysroot and runs `cargo metadata` on first attach (can take minutes on a large workspace) ‚Äî the canonical unavailability case the structural layer covers while it warms.

## 0.7.17 (2026-05-24)

### Added
- **Tree-sitter topology extraction for JavaScript (`.js`/`.mjs`/`.cjs`), split off the regex TS/JS extractor.** Plain JavaScript parses cleanly under gotreesitter ‚Äî it has none of the typed-arrow syntax that trips the missing TypeScript external lex-states table (see `docs/internal/treesitter-plan.md`) ‚Äî so it no longer needs the fragile regex scanner. New `treesitter.NewJavaScript`, registered as an `EngineTreeSitter` `javascript` row in `internal/langsupport` (owning `.js`/`.mjs`/`.cjs`) and wired into `buildExtractors`; the `typescript` regex row is narrowed to `.ts`/`.tsx`/`.jsx` only. It extracts top-level **functions** (declarations and arrow/function-expression bindings, including `export`ed ones), **classes** with their **methods** (lexical containment, 1.0/extractor), top-level **constants**/**variables** (`const` ‚Üí constant, `let`/`var` ‚Üí variable), ES `import` and CommonJS `require` **imports** (the module path), and `describe`/`it`/`test` blocks at any nesting depth (‚Üí `KindTest`). Intra-file **call edges** are name-resolved heuristics (0.8/heuristic), resolving calls inside functions, arrow bindings and methods. JavaScript probed clean (0 ERROR/0 MISSING) on an idiomatic multi-line sample. This is the cheap interim win of the (still-blocked) Phase 8 TS/TSX flip ‚Äî only `.ts`/`.tsx`/`.jsx` remain on regex. Tests in `internal/topology/extractors/treesitter/javascript_test.go`.

## 0.7.16 (2026-05-24)

### Added
- **Symbol tools keep working when the language server is cold or cannot parse the file (tree-sitter fallback).** `read_symbol`, `insert_before_symbol`, `insert_after_symbol` and `replace_symbol_body` now fall back to a **fresh tree-sitter parse** of the current file (via the topology index) when the LSP `documentSymbol` call errors or times out ‚Äî the symbol is located structurally and the operation proceeds, annotated `[topology fallback ‚Äî LSP unavailable; ‚Ä¶ range is line-granular]`. The new `Store.ExtractFile` re-parses the file *as it is on disk right now* (not the possibly-stale persisted index), so the resolved ranges are accurate; the edit application path already errors cleanly (never corrupts) on an out-of-range position, the tools remain **dry-run by default**, and the fallback only engages when the LSP path fails ‚Äî so the LSP-up behaviour is byte-for-byte unchanged. `safe_delete_symbol` deliberately has **no** fallback: its safety guarantee is the LSP reference check, which topology cannot reproduce. Wired via a nil-safe `WithTopologyFallback` setter on each tool (mirrors the existing query-tool fallbacks). Shared helpers in `internal/tools/symbol_topology_fallback.go`; tests in `symbol_topology_fallback_test.go` (read, replace incl. exact-bytes + dry-run, insert, and no-fallback-surfaces-error). This is the resilience half of the Phase 4 "byte-precise surgical edits" item; the char-precise doc-comment/signature/body sub-range separation (which would retire the `include_doc_comment` heuristic) is deferred ‚Äî it needs character-precise ranges in `topology.Node`, a schema change touching every extractor.

## 0.7.15 (2026-05-24)

### Changed
- **`topology_affected` is now the headline tool: recall-biased, confidence-labelled, and co-location-aware.** Previously it only walked inward dependency edges ‚Äî but the extractors emit *intra-file* call edges only, so a test in a sibling file (`foo_test.go` beside `foo.go`, `test_foo.py` beside `foo.py`) that exercises a changed symbol was not graph-connected and went unreported. It now adds a **co-location pass**: tests in the same directory as any changed or affected file are flagged too (new `Store.TestsInDirs`, matching on the immediate parent directory). Every affected test now carries a **confidence** and the **reason** it was flagged ‚Äî `1.0` certain (containment), `0.8` dependency edge, `0.5` co-located (same directory, no edge) ‚Äî and tests are ordered highest-confidence first.
